00:43:27","updatedTime":"2021-04-13 00:43:27","title":"How to Take a Panning Shot","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>A great panning shot, with the moving object in clear focus and the background blurred just right, convinces you that a still photograph is in motion. Consistently capturing superior panning shots takes time and practice, but it’s definitely a skill worth working on for any amateur photographer with a DSLR camera. Your results may be hit-or-miss at first, but your “hit” photographs will be fantastic! </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Take-a-Panning-Shot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Take-a-Panning-Shot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Camera Settings\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Camera-Settings\">Camera Settings</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Get a good DSLR camera to take true panning shots. A well-crafted panning shot puts the target image in extreme focus while blurring the background to create a sense of motion. The average smartphone camera or basic digital camera struggles to achieve this result. If you really want to capture great panning shots, your best bet is to <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Choose-a-DSLR-Camera\" title=\"Choose a DSLR Camera\">invest in a high-quality digital single-lens reflex (DSLR) camera</a>.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-1.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 1.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a2/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-1.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-1.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Unfortunately for your wallet, a good DSLR camera can easily cost $500 USD or more.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Set your camera to shutter priority mode for maximum shutter control. Shutter speed and responsiveness are critical to getting a good panning shot, since you need the right shutter speed to “freeze” your object in motion. Shutter priority mode gives you maximum shutter control, so turn the dial on your DSLR camera to the appropriate symbol; check your camera’s product manual for guidance.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/60/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-2.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, on Canon DSLR cameras, the shutter priority symbol is “Tv,” while it’s “S” on Nikon DSLRs.</li> \n    <li>Using shutter priority mode will probably result in automated settings for aperture and ISO values. Aperture controls the amount of light that reaches the camera sensor, with a lower number denoting more light and a higher number equating to more light. Increasing the ISO setting can also aid in brightness, but a higher ISO value results in more graininess (or “noise”) in your captured image. Both aperture and ISO are less essential than shutter speed when taking panning shots, but you can refer to your camera guide if you want options for fine-tuning these settings as well.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Start at a slower shutter speed and adjust it faster based on your results. Finding the right shutter speed is definitely a trial-and-error process. Start at a slower speed, in the 1/4 - 1/15 second range, and see how your first few photos turn out.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup> Increase the shutter speed as needed, with faster shutter speeds being required for faster moving objects.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup> Use the following as a general reference:\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-3.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 3.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/fb/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-3.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-3.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Walking at a normal pace: 1/2 - 1/4 sec.</li> \n    <li>Runner or average cyclist: 1/4 - 1/15 sec.</li> \n    <li>Fast cyclist or car in street traffic: 1/15 - 1/30 sec.</li> \n    <li>Racing car: 1/60 - 1/125 sec.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Turn off any image stabilization setting unless it has advanced features. While image stabilization is a great feature when you’re holding the camera still, it will typically try to “correct” the camera movement that’s essential to panning shots. Use image stabilization only if your camera has an advanced type that recognizes and doesn’t interfere with panning shots.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/ee/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-4.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Use your product manual to learn about your camera’s image stabilization feature and how to turn it off.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Use autofocus for simplicity when you’re new to taking panning shots. Many action photography pros prefer manual focus for panning shots, but autofocus is the easier option when you’re less experienced. Using your camera’s autofocus setting requires less active effort on your part, since the camera continuously refocuses on the target object. That said, autofocus usually adjusts more slowly than is possible with manual focus, so you’re sacrificing greater control for greater ease of use.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/43/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-5.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Advance to manual focus, if desired, once your skills improve. There’s no rule that says you have to switch from autofocus to manual focus as you get more experience taking panning shots, but it’s probably worth a try. As opposed to autofocus, manual focus requires you to estimate and pre-sight the focal point for the object, which can be a definite challenge for a novice. If you get it right, though, manual focus is more responsive and—at least in skilled hands—more likely to capture a clear image.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/58/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-6.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Utilize burst/continuous mode to improve your chances of a great shot. Without burst mode, also called continuous mode, you’ll get one chance to capture a great photo each time your target passes by. With burst mode, which takes numerous photos in rapid succession, you’ll often get 10 or more chances for a perfect pic each time you press the shutter button.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/f3/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-7.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Most modern DSLR cameras have burst mode. Check your product guide for details.</li> \n    <li>The only real downside to burst mode? You’ll end up with a lot of out-of-focus shots to delete!</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Switch lenses, if needed, based on your positioning and photo preferences. Follow the specific instructions for your camera, but expect something similar to the following: hold down the lens release button throughout the entire process; turn the current lens clockwise to remove it; line up the dots on the camera and the new lens; turn the new lens counterclockwise until it clicks into place.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-8.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 8.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/55/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-8.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-8.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Which <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Choose-Lenses-for-a-Camera\" title=\"Choose Lenses for a Camera\">lens you choose</a> depends on factors like your expected distance from the target object and how wide or narrow you want to focus in. You might, for example, switch to a wide-angle (24-35 mm) lens to capture a passing bicycle as a small image amidst a large background. Or, you might use a telephoto (70-135+ mm) lens to zoom in almost exclusively on the passing bicycle.</li> \n    <li>Your positioning for the shot and your lens selection are a tandem deal. Decide on both at the same time.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Take-a-Panning-Shot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Positioning\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Positioning\">Positioning</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Set up safely at a distance that coordinates with your lens selection. Find a spot with a clear view that doesn’t put you in harm’s way, so that the object will pass directly in front of you. If you’re using a telephoto lens, you might set up away to get a great shot of a running herd of deer, for example, or you might use a wide angle lens and set up away from a passing bicycle to capture the city backdrop as well.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-9.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 9.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/67/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-9.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-9.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Always take your safety and the safety of those around you into account. Make sure you’re not exposed to vehicle or pedestrian traffic, for instance. Use a second person as a spotter if you’re taking pictures in a risky environment, such as at a racetrack.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Steady your camera by attaching a <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Attach-a-Camera-to-a-Tripod\" title=\"Attach a Camera to a Tripod\">tripod</a> or monopod to it. Keeping your camera steady and level is important when you're taking panning shots.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup> While pros can often free-hand their panning shots, start out by attaching your camera to a 3-leg tripod or a 1-leg monopod. Most tripods and monopods have a camera plate that screws into the threaded opening at the bottom of your camera; the plate then slides and locks into place on the tripod/monopod.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-10.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 10.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/ed/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-10.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-10.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Tripods are a bit bulkier, but are probably the best choice if you’re a novice. A monopod requires more balance and support on your part.</li> \n    <li>Once you’re comfortable taking panning shots, practice doing them without a tripod or monopod. Overall, tripods and monopods are particularly helpful when the target (like a car) follows a predictable path. Free-shooting without a tripod/monopod is useful when the target (such as an animal) is moving less predictably.<sup id=\"_ref-15\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 15\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-15\">[15]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Create a solid base from your hips down so you can rotate at the waist. This is important even when you’re using a tripod or monopod. Set your legs shoulder-width apart and bend your knees slightly. Point your toes, knees, and hips straight forward so that they’ll be pointed right at your target as it passes by you. Your lower body should remain in this position throughout the panning process—all of your body movement should come from above your hips.<sup id=\"_ref-16\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 16\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-16\">[16]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-11.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 11.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/f3/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-11.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-11.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Some photographers find it easier to point their lower body a bit in the direction from which the moving target will approach, and still others prefer to point slightly in the direction to which the target will exit the panning area. This is really up to your personal preference and comfort level. The important thing is to keep your lower body steady and still.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Visualize a target zone of about 60 degrees to your left and right. Imagine you’re standing in the middle of a clock face. Your lower body, then, is pointed at 12 o’clock. That means your target zone (or panning zone) should range from 10 o’clock to 2 o’clock (or 2 to 10, if the object is approaching from your right). To get a great panning shot, you’ll need to track your target object from one end of this zone to the other.<sup id=\"_ref-17\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 17\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-17\">[17]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-12.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 12.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/93/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-12.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-12.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, say you’re trying to get a panning shot of your daughter riding her bike from your left to your right. While keeping your lower body pointed at 12 o’clock, you’ll need to turn your upper body to start tracking her at 10 o’clock, and continue to turn and track her all the way to 2 o’clock.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Pre-sight your expected focal point if you’re using manual focus. If you’re relying on manual focus, estimate the spot where you expect your target to pass by at the 12 o’clock position. Focus your camera on that point, and maintain that focus setting as you track the target object. That way, when the object passes by you, it will (hopefully) be in perfect focus!<sup id=\"_ref-18\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 18\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-18\">[18]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-13.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 13.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/59/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-13.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-13.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you’re using autofocus, don’t worry about this step. The camera will adjust its focus “on the fly.”</li> \n    <li>Like many aspects of taking panning shots, expect to go through some trial-and-error here.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Take-a-Panning-Shot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Shooting\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Shooting\">Shooting</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Aim your camera and upper body at the starting point of your target zone. In other words, if the car you want to photograph is approaching from your right, point your upper body and the camera at the 2 o’clock position. Watch through the viewfinder and wait for the target to enter the frame.<sup id=\"_ref-19\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 19\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-19\">[19]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-14.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 14.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e1/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-14.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-14.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Remember to keep your lower body still and pointed at 12 o’clock. Doing so will help you swivel the camera through the target zone smoothly.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Press the button halfway down to autofocus on the approaching target. As the target enters your view, engage the autofocus to train in on it. If you’re using manual focus instead of autofocus, keep the shutter button pressed halfway down to maintain the focal point you already established.<sup id=\"_ref-20\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 20\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-20\">[20]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-15.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 15.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/2f/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-15.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-15.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you’re using an unfamiliar camera, practice pressing on the shutter button beforehand so you know how much pressure to apply.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Center the moving object in your frame as you track it through the target zone. Start rotating your upper body as soon as the target enters your view. Do your best to match its speed and keep it centered in the frame. If you’re using autofocus, the camera will keep adjusting as you go. If you’re using manual focus, the target should increasingly come into focus as it approaches the 12 o’clock position.<sup id=\"_ref-21\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 21\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-21\">[21]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-16.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 16.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e5/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-16.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-16.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>The faster your target is moving, the harder this is to master. Consider practicing on neighborhood joggers before moving up to competitive sprinters!</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Take the shot right as the target passes by you. Wait until the target is centered in the frame at the 12 o’clock position to press down fully on the shutter button. This is the ideal position to take your panning shot.<sup id=\"_ref-22\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 22\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-22\">[22]</a></sup> But don’t feel bad if you miss-time your shot the first few times—keep trying and you’ll get it!<sup id=\"_ref-23\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 23\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-23\">[23]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-17.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 17.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/53/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-17.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-17.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Your entire body should be aligned with the target at this point.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Track the moving object with your camera until it exits the target zone. Don’t stop twisting your body and tracking the target after taking your shot! Just like with a golf swing, your follow-through is a critical component. Keep turning your upper body and tracking the target until it exits your panning zone—for instance, the 10 o’clock position if it’s moving from your right to your left.<sup id=\"_ref-24\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 24\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-24\">[24]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-18.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Take a Panning Shot Step 18.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/80/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-18.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-18.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you’re using burst mode, your camera will take several shots as you continue to track the target. But even if you’re not using burst mode, following through will greatly improve your odds of getting a great panning shot. Following through helps add to the background blur effect that is key to expressing motion in a panning shot.</li> \n    <li>If you capture a great panning shot on your first attempt, give yourself a pat on the back! But don’t be surprised or disappointed if your first few efforts don’t quite work out.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Take-a-Panning-Shot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Taking good panning shots takes practice! Before trying to get great shots at a racetrack, practice with slower-moving targets in a low-stress environment, like walkers and joggers in your neighborhood.<sup id=\"_ref-25\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 25\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Take-a-Panning-Shot#_note-25\">[25]</a></sup></li> \n  <li>The interchangeable lenses on a DSLR camera are defined primarily by their focal length (mm) and aperture (f/). The smaller the focal length number, the wider the shot you can capture; the smaller the aperture number, the less light is required to get a good shot.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Take-a-Panning-Shot&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: References\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"References\">References</span></h2>\n <div class=\"mw-references-wrap </li> \n  </ol>\n </div> \n</div>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 12 Apr 2021 00:00:00 +0000","feedId":44,"bgimg":"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a2/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-1.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-1.jpg","linkMd5":"8548c306b5f099b5dfa7cf3943f15e3b","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn48@2020_6/2021/04/12/16-43-43-208_37348ed451f14c33.webp","destWidth":728,"destHeight":546,"sourceBytes":48303,"destBytes":30266,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a2/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-1.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-1.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn48@2020_6/2021/04/12/16-43-43-208_37348ed451f14c33.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/60/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-2.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn92@2020_2/2021/04/12/16-44-05-128_1cba90affc0efff7.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/fb/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-3.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-3.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn43@2020_2/2021/04/12/16-43-49-095_28d58aae458069d0.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/ee/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-4.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-4.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn47@2020_6/2021/04/12/16-43-48-862_d64665ea876aab43.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/43/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-5.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-5.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn47@2020_6/2021/04/12/16-43-48-038_8b32c86491af1fdd.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/58/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-6.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-6.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn28@2020_3/2021/04/12/16-44-06-182_5b5b46cb47e415d4.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/f3/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-7.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-7.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn95@2020_6/2021/04/12/16-43-48-110_8da3581b4608c1cc.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/55/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-8.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-8.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn68@2020_1/2021/04/12/16-43-57-232_7ac5d65dae8b562f.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/67/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-9.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-9.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn98@2020_4/2021/04/12/16-43-49-402_0efb9a1f303330bc.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/ed/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-10.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-10.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn43@2020_2/2021/04/12/16-43-49-553_eaa24306813078cc.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/f3/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-11.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-11.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn27@2020_5/2021/04/12/16-43-47-720_77eb11f071dd2561.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/93/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-12.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-12.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn24@2020_4/2021/04/12/16-43-48-075_af64bb23c313f0e4.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/59/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-13.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-13.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn60@2020_5/2021/04/12/16-43-48-918_a8e1cf461176db12.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e1/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-14.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-14.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn31@2020_3/2021/04/12/16-43-48-831_48e946693e632bdb.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/2f/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-15.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-15.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn71@2020_6/2021/04/12/16-43-48-006_ddd829df22825397.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e5/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-16.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-16.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn51@2020_6/2021/04/12/16-43-50-315_376a3c3e4e36a02f.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/53/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-17.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-17.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn36@2020_6/2021/04/12/16-43-48-843_2ebedeaa01539624.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/80/Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-18.jpg/aid12311753-v4-728px-Take-a-Panning-Shot-Step-18.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn39@2020_2/2021/04/12/16-43-57-370_d1599d0315600ce2.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1618245807332},{"createdTime":"2021-04-13 00:43:27","updatedTime":"2021-04-13 00:43:27","title":"How to Measure Room Temperature","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Measure-Room-Temperature","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>Room temperature refers to the range of air temperatures that people prefer indoors. Measuring room temperature is actually really easy to do. You can choose a thermometer that you keep in the center of the room to provide a temperature reading, or you can download an app to your smartphone that can measure room temperature. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Measure-Room-Temperature&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Measure-Room-Temperature&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Reading a Thermometer\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Reading-a-Thermometer\">Reading a Thermometer</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Choose a digital thermometer for the most accurate reading. Electronic or digital thermometers can be more expensive than other thermometers, but they provide a faster reading and can give a more accurate temperature. They also react to temperature changes faster than other types of thermometers so you always have an accurate reading.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Measure-Room-Temperature#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-1.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Measure Room Temperature Step 1.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/97/Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-1.jpg/aid11180313-v4-728px-Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-1.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Some digital thermometers have the capability to store temperature readings. So you can compare the room temperature over time to see how it changes.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Use a glass thermometer to get an approximate temperature. Glass thermometers use a glass tube filled with liquid to measure the temperature. As the air around the thermometer gets warmer, the liquid moves up the tube and can be used to get a close measurement of the room temperature.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Measure Room Temperature Step 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/46/Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-2.jpg/aid11180313-v4-728px-Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Choose a glass thermometer that doesn’t contain mercury. Mercury is highly toxic and can be dangerous if the thermometer breaks.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Measure-Room-Temperature#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup></li> \n    <li>Glass thermometers can also be called a bulb thermometer or a liquid-in-glass thermometer.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Select a bimetallic thermometer for an easy to read option. Bimetallic or dial thermometers have a metal pointer that moves up and down a circular scale to show you the temperature. They use a strip of metal that expands and bends as the temperature increases. As the strip expands or contracts, it moves the pointer on the scale. The big arrow of the pointer makes it easy to check the room temperature.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Measure-Room-Temperature#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-3.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Measure Room Temperature Step 3.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/27/Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-3.jpg/aid11180313-v4-728px-Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-3.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Bimetallic thermometers aren’t as accurate as digital thermometers.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Place the thermometer in the center of the room. No matter what type of thermometer you use, you need to place it in the center of the room at least off of the ground for an accurate measurement of room temperature. Mounting a thermometer on a wall can produce inaccurate results because the heat from the walls can distort the reading.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Measure-Room-Temperature#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-4-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Measure Room Temperature Step 4 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/9f/Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-4-Version-2.jpg/aid11180313-v4-728px-Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-4-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Set the thermometer on a table or stool so the temperature of the floor doesn’t affect the reading.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Wait 5 minutes for the thermometer to adjust to the room. Before you check the temperature, allow the thermometer to adjust to the room. Thermometers, especially glass and bimetallic, need a few minutes to accurately read the temperature of the room.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Measure Room Temperature Step 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/3b/Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-5.jpg/aid11180313-v4-728px-Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Don’t hold or stand directly next to the thermometer or your body heat could affect the temperature reading.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Measure-Room-Temperature#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Check the temperature on the thermometer. After you’ve placed your thermometer in the center of the room and waited a few minutes to allow it to adjust, you can check the temperature reading to measure the room temperature. A general room temperature measurement is around .<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Measure-Room-Temperature#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Measure Room Temperature Step 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/44/Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-6.jpg/aid11180313-v4-728px-Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>A digital thermometer will display the temperature on its screen and will be the most accurate.</li> \n    <li>Read the numbers next to the top of the liquid in a glass thermometer to measure the temperature.</li> \n    <li>Look at the number that the arrow is pointing to on a bimetallic thermometer to measure the temperature.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Measure-Room-Temperature&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Using a Smartphone\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Using-a-Smartphone\">Using a Smartphone</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Download a thermometer application to your smartphone. Many smartphones are equipped with sensors that they use to monitor the temperature of the device. You can download an app that uses these sensors to take an ambient temperature reading of the room. Go to the app store on your phone and search for a thermometer app to download.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Measure-Room-Temperature#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Measure Room Temperature Step 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/79/Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-7.jpg/aid11180313-v4-728px-Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Go to the app store to <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Download-Free-Apps-on-App-Store\" title=\"Download Free Apps on App Store\">download a thermometer app to your iPhone</a>.</li> \n    <li>Use the Google Play Store to <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Download-Free-Apps-on-Android\" title=\"Download Free Apps on Android\">download an app to your Android</a>.</li> \n    <li>Popular temperature apps include My Thermometer, Smart Thermometer, and iThermometer.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Open the application. Once you’ve downloaded the app, locate it on your screen, and tap on it with your finger to open it up. You may have to wait a few minutes for the app to update after you open it up.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-8.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Measure Room Temperature Step 8.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/d6/Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-8.jpg/aid11180313-v4-728px-Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-8.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You have to wait until the app is fully downloaded before you can open it.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Select the ambient temperature reading to measure room temperature. Depending on which app you use, you will have different temperature readings to choose from. Some apps allow you to check the temperature of your phone’s battery or the temperature outside based on meteorological data. Choose the ambient temperature reading to find the room temperature around you.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Measure-Room-Temperature#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-9.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Measure Room Temperature Step 9.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e8/Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-9.jpg/aid11180313-v4-728px-Measure-Room-Temperature-Step-9.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Measure-Room-Temperature&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: References\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"References\">References</span></h2>\n <div class=\"mw-references-wrap\">\n  <ol class=\"references\"> \n   <li <p>Amazon is simple to use and a great place to find almost anything you need. There are also a ton of ways you can get discounts and save money. Like the site itself, many of the deals and discounts are easy to find if you know what you’re looking for. To make it easy for you, we’ve put together a handy list of ways you can take advantage of all of the deals and discounts on Amazon so you can save as much money as possible. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Get-Discounts-On-Amazon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Get-Discounts-On-Amazon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Become a Prime member.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Become-a-Prime-member.\">Become a Prime member.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Shop the exclusive deals that come with it. Amazon Prime is Amazon’s membership program that allows you to take advantage of exclusive deals and discounts such as flash sales and Amazon Prime Day, an annual shopping holiday available only to Prime members. Visit the Amazon homepage and choose the option to sign up for a Prime membership. It’s free for 30 days and then it costs $12 a month, but you can pay an annual fee of $119 for a better deal.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-1-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Get Discounts On Amazon Step 1 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/73/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-1-Version-5.jpg/aid2780536-v4-728px-Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-1-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you have Amazon Prime, you also have access to their entertainment services such as Prime Video and Prime Music.</li> \n    <li>Join Amazon Prime by visiting: <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/58f8026f-0658-47d0-9752-f6fa2c69b2e2/qualify?_encoding=UTF8&amp;merchant=\">https://www.amazon.com/58f8026f-0658-47d0-9752-f6fa2c69b2e2/qualify?_encoding=UTF8&amp;merchant=</a>.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Get-Discounts-On-Amazon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Apply for an Amazon Prime Rewards Card.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Apply-for-an-Amazon-Prime-Rewards-Card.\">Apply for an Amazon Prime Rewards Card.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Earn money and get cash back whenever you use your credit card. Whenever you purchase items at Amazon.com or at Whole Foods, you can earn 5% back. If you use the card at restaurants, gas stations, and drugstores you can earn 2% back. For all other purchases that you make with your card, you’ll earn 1% back, so no matter what, you’ll always be earning cash back! Visit the Amazon website and fill out the application to apply for the card.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-2-Version-3.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Get Discounts On Amazon Step 2 Version 3.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/68/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-2-Version-3.jpg/aid2780536-v4-728px-Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-2-Version-3.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Apply for an Amazon Prime Rewards Card here: <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Amazon-Prime-Rewards-Visa-Signature-Card/dp/BT00LN946S\">https://www.amazon.com/Amazon-Prime-Rewards-Visa-Signature-Card/dp/BT00LN946S</a>.</li> \n    <li>Keep in mind that the rewards card is a credit card, and you’ll need to have a high enough credit score in order to be approved.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Get-Discounts-On-Amazon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Join Amazon Family if you need stuff for your kids.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Join-Amazon-Family-if-you-need-stuff-for-your-kids.\">Join Amazon Family if you need stuff for your kids.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Get discounts and age-specific deals. If you plan to use Amazon for things like diapers, baby registries, or for products for your children, sign up for Amazon Family. You’ll get access to discounts on family-related subscriptions and deals that are tailored for you and your family. If you’re a college student, visit the Amazon page and choose the Amazon Prime Student option. Fill out the information to confirm that you’re a student and start taking advantage of the benefits of Prime for free, including Prime Video, Amazon Music, Prime Photos, and free two-day shipping.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-4-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Get Discounts On Amazon Step 4 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/83/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-4-Version-5.jpg/aid2780536-v4-728px-Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-4-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>In order to verify that you’re a student, you’ll need to upload a scan or image of your student ID, a transcript or class list with your name on it, your tuition bill with your name on it, or an official acceptance letter for the upcoming term.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Get-Discounts-On-Amazon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Click on the “Today’s Deals” page.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span id=\"Click-on-the-“Today’s-Deals”-page.\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Click-on-the-.E2.80.9CToday.E2.80.99s-Deals.E2.80.9D-page.\">Click on the “Today’s Deals” page.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Take advantage of limited-time discounts. Amazon maintains a page dedicated to deals and discounted items. It’s updated on a daily basis so click on the link and take a look through the items to see if there’s anything you’re interested in. Snag any discounted items you want while they’re priced low.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-5-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Get Discounts On Amazon Step 5 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/34/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-5-Version-5.jpg/aid2780536-v4-728px-Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-5-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Visit Amazon’s Today’s Deals page here: <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/goldbox?ref_=nav_cs_gb_8b76f3deb4464058af8eb975e65f885d\">https://www.amazon.com/gp/goldbox?ref_=nav_cs_gb_8b76f3deb4464058af8eb975e65f885d</a>.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Get-Discounts-On-Amazon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: Use Amazon Coupons on specific items.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Use-Amazon-Coupons-on-specific-items.\">Use Amazon Coupons on specific items.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Save the digital coupons and use them at checkout. Click on the Amazon Coupons page and take a look through it. Keep an eye out for coupons that will work on items that you buy a lot or on items that you’re interested in purchasing. Click on the “Clip Coupon” option to save the digital coupon to your cart so they can be automatically applied when you check out.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-6-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Get Discounts On Amazon Step 6 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/3e/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-6-Version-5.jpg/aid2780536-v4-728px-Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-6-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>To visit Amazon Coupons, go to this page: <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Coupons/b/?ie=UTF8&amp;node=2231352011&amp;ref=insider_ar_tips_dlssvngs\">https://www.amazon.com/Coupons/b/?ie=UTF8&amp;node=2231352011&amp;ref=insider_ar_tips_dlssvngs</a>.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Get-Discounts-On-Amazon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8\" title=\"Edit section: Choose “Subscribe and Save” for repeat buys.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span id=\"Choose-“Subscribe-and-Save”-for-repeat-buys.\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Choose-.E2.80.9CSubscribe-and-Save.E2.80.9D-for-repeat-buys.\">Choose “Subscribe and Save” for repeat buys.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>If you buy certain items regularly, use this feature to save money. If you purchase an item or product on a regular basis, whether it’s weekly or monthly, you can save up to 15% simply by using Amazon’s Subscribe and Save service. Choose the option to “subscribe” to the item and set how many and how often you want them shipped to you.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-7-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Get Discounts On Amazon Step 7 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/98/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-7-Version-5.jpg/aid2780536-v4-728px-Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-7-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For instance, if you buy a bag of dog food once every month, you might as well sign up for the feature to save some money on it! You can choose to have 1 bag sent to you each month.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Get-Discounts-On-Amazon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9\" title=\"Edit section: Check out Amazon Warehouse Deals.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Check-out-Amazon-Warehouse-Deals.\">Check out Amazon Warehouse Deals.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Look through the open box and used products for reduced prices. The Amazon Outlets hub features items that have had their prices reduced in an effort to get them sold. Avoid paying full price for items by checking through the page for things that you like. Browse different filter options for different items and deals.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-9-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Get Discounts On Amazon Step 9 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/ab/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-9-Version-5.jpg/aid2780536-v4-728px-Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-9-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>To browse Amazon Outlets, visit <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Outlet/b?ie=UTF8&amp;node=517808\">https://www.amazon.com/Outlet/b?ie=UTF8&amp;node=517808</a>.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Get-Discounts-On-Amazon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11\" title=\"Edit section: Choose the no-rush shipping option.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Choose-the-no-rush-shipping-option.\">Choose the no-rush shipping option.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>If you don’t mind the wait, you can save some money. The standard shipping charge from Amazon guarantees that your items will arrive within 2 days. But if you don’t mind potentially waiting an extra day or so, you can choose the option for free, no-rush shipping. You’ll immediately receive a discount on your order or a reward to your account once your order ships.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-11-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Get Discounts On Amazon Step 11 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/81/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-11-Version-5.jpg/aid2780536-v4-728px-Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-11-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Amazon defines “no-rush” as within 6 business days. So if you don’t mind waiting about a week, you can get a nice discount.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Get-Discounts-On-Amazon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12\" title=\"Edit section: Convert old gift cards.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Convert-old-gift-cards.\">Convert old gift cards.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Turn them into Amazon gift cards you can use. If have some old gift cards lying around such as Visa or Express gift cards, you can convert them into Amazon gift cards. Log into Amazon and visit the eGift Card page. Enter your gift card info and apply it to an Amazon gift card that you can use on the site.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-12-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Get Discounts On Amazon Step 12 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/09/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-12-Version-4.jpg/aid2780536-v4-728px-Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-12-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For instance, if you have a bunch of old gift cards with low balances on them, you can combine them all into an Amazon gift card.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Get-Discounts-On-Amazon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13\" title=\"Edit section: Set up a bonus on your reloadable gift card.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Set-up-a-bonus-on-your-reloadable-gift-card.\">Set up a bonus on your reloadable gift card.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Get a 2% bonus whenever you reload and use it. If you have an Amazon gift card, you can reload it and add more money to the balance. Whenever you do, you can earn a 2% bonus. Use the debit card that’s linked to your account and the extra bonus will be added to the gift card’s balance whenever you reload it.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-13-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Get Discounts On Amazon Step 13 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/1c/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-13-Version-4.jpg/aid2780536-v4-728px-Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-13-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can also earn a 2% bonus whenever you reload an Amazon gift card that you’ve given to someone else!</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Get-Discounts-On-Amazon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14\" title=\"Edit section: Use an online coupon site.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Use-an-online-coupon-site.\">Use an online coupon site.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Enter coupon codes to get discounts on certain items. There are a bunch of coupon sites such as Groupon, The Krazy Coupon Lady, and Coupons.com. Visit them and look for coupons that you can use on items that you buy from Amazon. Grab the coupon’s discount code and apply it to your Amazon order at checkout to save some extra money on your purchase.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-14-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Get Discounts On Amazon Step 14 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/16/Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-14-Version-4.jpg/aid2780536-v4-728px-Get-Discounts-On-Amazon-Step-14-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Additionally, there are groups on social media sites like Facebook that are dedicated to finding deals on Amazon. You can join them and take advantage of the deals that interest you.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Get-Discounts-On-Amazon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Keep in mind that deals are constantly updating on Amazon. So if you want something, but it’s too expensive, you can try checking back on it later.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Get-Discounts-On-Amazon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16\" title=\"Edit section: Warnings\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Warnings\">Warnings</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Be careful about giving out your financial information online, especially on other websites that aren’t secure like Amazon.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\"
