00:43:27","updatedTime":"2021-04-13 00:43:27","title":"How to Create Study Plans","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>Whether you're a university student or simply learning something new on your own, study time is crucial if you want to do well in your classes. With a study plan, the time you need simply becomes a part of your day so you don't have to worry about an exam or deadline sneaking up on you. The process can seem daunting if you haven't made your own study plan before, but never fear! We've compiled all the most useful tips for you to get the most out of your study time. We'll start with advice on how to work studying into your schedule, then give you some bonus tips on how to structure each study session to max out your productivity. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Carve out time to study every day.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Carve-out-time-to-study-every-day.\">Carve out time to study every day.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Set aside at least a couple of hours as dedicated study time. If you have a full day of classes and work, you might not have more than an hour or two each day to study. Use the weekend to catch up! If your schedule doesn't leave open a full 2-hour block on any particular day, look for spots where you can sneak in smaller 20-30 minute blocks.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Create-Study-Plans-Step-2-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Create Study Plans Step 2 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/d4/Create-Study-Plans-Step-2-Version-2.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-2-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, you might study for an hour in the morning, a half-hour at lunchtime, and another half-hour in the afternoon before work.</li> \n    <li>If you're working while going to school, include your study plan on your school schedule and let your manager know that you're not available for work during those times.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Schedule backward from exams and deadlines.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Schedule-backward-from-exams-and-deadlines.\">Schedule backward from exams and deadlines.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Put your exams and deadlines on your calendar when you get your syllabus. If you're taking several classes, you can easily see if you have several exams on the same day or projects due at the same time. Then, plan your study time backward from those dates to make sure you have enough time to get everything ready.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Create-Study-Plans-Step-6-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Create Study Plans Step 6 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/65/Create-Study-Plans-Step-6-Version-2.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-6-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Plan on getting papers and other assignments done early so you have time to edit and polish them before you turn them in. This also helps you avoid the stress of trying to do the entire thing at the last minute.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Include enough study time each week for each class.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Include-enough-study-time-each-week-for-each-class.\">Include enough study time each week for each class.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>The general rule is to study for 3 hours for every credit hour of the class. Use this rule to create your study plan before classes start. As you get into your classes, you might find that some of them require more study time while others require less.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Create-Study-Plans-Step-3-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Create Study Plans Step 3 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/77/Create-Study-Plans-Step-3-Version-2.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-3-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, if you're taking a Spanish class for 3 credit hours, schedule 9 hours of study for that class each week.</li> \n    <li>If a subject comes easily to you or you're taking a class that's mostly a review of stuff you already know, you can probably get away with less time studying.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Study at around the same time every day.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Study-at-around-the-same-time-every-day.\">Study at around the same time every day.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Your brain will be more focused if you commit to a regular schedule. After a week or two, you'll get in the habit of studying at that time, the same as you get used to having classes at a certain time. If you're going to school full-time, think of your school day as a workday and schedule study time in between classes to get the most out of your day.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Create-Study-Plans-Step-4-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Create Study Plans Step 4 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/7d/Create-Study-Plans-Step-4-Version-2.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-4-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you have seasonal activities, plan your study schedule around those activities even when they're not going on. For example, suppose you play intramural soccer during the spring, with practice on Mondays and games on Thursdays. Schedule your study time so it doesn't conflict, then you won't have to change your study plan when soccer starts.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Use your syllabus to plan each study session.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Use-your-syllabus-to-plan-each-study-session.\">Use your syllabus to plan each study session.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Set specific tasks to do each study session using action words. Think of your syllabus as a roadmap to guide your study sessions until the end of the course. Note when lectures are and what you're supposed to do to prepare, then add in time to review your lecture notes before you prepare for the next class session.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Create-Study-Plans-Step-5-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Create Study Plans Step 5 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/01/Create-Study-Plans-Step-5-Version-2.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-5-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, suppose you have a history class on Tuesdays and Thursdays. Your instructor assigns reading to prepare for the class. Your study plan might be to read for 1 hour on Monday, review lecture notes for 15 minutes on Tuesday, read for 1 hour on Wednesday, then review lecture notes for 15 minutes on Thursday.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: Break up larger assignments.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Break-up-larger-assignments.\">Break up larger assignments.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Do smaller parts of larger assignments over a longer period. Working backward from the due date, plan out blocks when you'll work on specific segments of a larger assignment. Use the week of the due date to bring those parts together and do the final polishing of your assignment so it's ready to turn in.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Create-Study-Plans-Step-7-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Create Study Plans Step 7 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/9f/Create-Study-Plans-Step-7-Version-2.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-7-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, if you have a research paper due in 3 weeks, you might research the first week, write the first draft the second week, then edit and proofread the week the paper's due.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8\" title=\"Edit section: Study the most difficult things first.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Study-the-most-difficult-things-first.\">Study the most difficult things first.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Do more challenging things when your mind is fresh. When you sit down to study a subject, start with whatever part is giving you the most trouble. Dedicate as much of your time to that thing as you feel like you need to before moving on.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Create-Study-Plans-Step-8-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Create Study Plans Step 8 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/41/Create-Study-Plans-Step-8-Version-2.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-8-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you manage to conquer something that was giving you trouble before, you'll feel more motivated to tackle easier parts of the material.</li> \n    <li>While you don't want to completely neglect material you feel confident about, a quick review is usually all you'll need to keep it fresh if you feel like you already know it well.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9\" title=\"Edit section: Plan for regular breaks to maintain focus.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Plan-for-regular-breaks-to-maintain-focus.\">Plan for regular breaks to maintain focus.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Study for 25 minutes then take a 5-minute break. This tactic is known as the Pomodoro Technique and helps you maintain peak focus. When you take your break, though, remember to actually take a real break for the entire 5 minutes. Get up and walk around, do jumping jacks, get a snack, text friends, or watch cat videos on YouTube—whatever you need to give your brain a rest!<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Create-Study-Plans-Step-9.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Create Study Plans Step 9.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/96/Create-Study-Plans-Step-9.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-9.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>This isn't just goofing off—without regular breaks, your brain will internalize less of what you study. Taking frequent breaks helps you get the most out of your study sessions.</li> \n    <li>Keeping your study blocks short also helps you stay on task because you know a break is coming up soon. It's easy for your mind to wander if you've been sitting and staring at the same material for an hour.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10\" title=\"Edit section: Review as soon after class as possible.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Review-as-soon-after-class-as-possible.\">Review as soon after class as possible.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Go over what you covered in class as soon as possible to cement it in your brain. Look over your lecture notes, then try writing a brief summary of what you talked about in class. Think about what you would say if someone asked you what you talked about in class today. Usually, about 15 minutes is sufficient for a review.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Create-Study-Plans-Step-10.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Create Study Plans Step 10.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/05/Create-Study-Plans-Step-10.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-10.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, if you have 2 classes on Mondays, Wednesdays, and Fridays, you might plan a half-hour study session on those evenings to go over what you covered in each class that day.</li> \n    <li>Go through your notes and fill in any areas that might be hard to understand or difficult to read. For example, if you were writing really fast, your notes might be illegible if you don't go back to them for several weeks.</li> \n    <li>Reviewing soon after class can also help you identify concepts you don't understand or questions you might have for your instructor. That way, you can send them an email or take advantage of their office hours to get an answer immediately, rather than waiting until right before the exam.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11\" title=\"Edit section: Add a cumulative review every week.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Add-a-cumulative-review-every-week.\">Add a cumulative review every week.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Read through your notes for each class at least once a week. It's easy to forget what you've learned when you're constantly learning new things each week. Creating an outline for your class is a good way to do a cumulative review. Then, all you have to do is go over your outline each week.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Create-Study-Plans-Step-11.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Create Study Plans Step 11.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/71/Create-Study-Plans-Step-11.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-11.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, if you're taking 4 classes, you might schedule a 2-hour study block on Saturdays in which you spend 30 minutes doing a cumulative review for each class.</li> \n    <li>Cumulative review also helps you understand how the later things you learn build on the earlier things you learned. You'll likely notice new connections between parts of the class that you wouldn't have noticed otherwise.</li> \n    <li>This is especially important for classes that have a cumulative final exam. If you've done a cumulative review every week, you'll have a lot less work to do to get ready for that big final.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12\" title=\"Edit section: Include extra study sessions before exams.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Include-extra-study-sessions-before-exams.\">Include extra study sessions before exams.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Look for blank spaces in your regular schedule that can be used for exam study. In addition to your regular study time, you might want to study more in the week or so before an exam. Instead of taking away from study time for other classes, add more study blocks that you can dedicate to exam preparation.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Create-Study-Plans-Step-12.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Create Study Plans Step 12.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/34/Create-Study-Plans-Step-12.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-12.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, suppose you have a chemistry exam coming up. You normally study chemistry for an hour on Mondays, Wednesdays, and Fridays, then for 2 hours on Saturday. If you have free time on Tuesdays and Thursdays, you might add an hour of study on those days the week before the exam.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13\" title=\"Edit section: Evaluate your plan regularly and tweak it if necessary.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Evaluate-your-plan-regularly-and-tweak-it-if-necessary.\">Evaluate your plan regularly and tweak it if necessary.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Increase or decrease study time based on your grades and class performance. If you start to feel like you're really struggling in one class, figure out where you can make more time to study for that class. You might also want to try different study methods if what you're doing isn't working, such as joining a study group or going to the professor's office hours.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Create-Study-Plans-Step-14.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Create Study Plans Step 14.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/43/Create-Study-Plans-Step-14.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-14.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you had an exam for a class that you thought was easy and you did really well on, you probably don't have to study as much for that one. Take some study time from the easy class and use it for one you find more challenging.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14\" title=\"Edit section: Use group study sessions to prepare for exams.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Use-group-study-sessions-to-prepare-for-exams.\">Use group study sessions to prepare for exams.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Work with classmates as it gets closer to exam time. If you're weak in one area, chances are there's someone else in the class who's strong in that same area and can help you understand it. If you've got something down, teaching it to someone who doesn't helps you understand it even better.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Create-Study-Plans-Step-13.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Create Study Plans Step 13.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/02/Create-Study-Plans-Step-13.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-13.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>In classes where problem-solving and thinking are important, working in groups is an asset because you can learn different ways of thinking and approaching problems that you might not have thought of on your own.</li> \n    <li>Even if you don't think you work well in groups, give a study group a chance—especially if it's your first year in university—just to see if you get anything out of it. You can always drop the group if you don't feel like you're getting any benefit from it.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15\" title=\"Edit section: Set up a dedicated study area.\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Set-up-a-dedicated-study-area.\">Set up a dedicated study area.</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Choose a well-lit, comfortable spot where you can focus and concentrate. It's usually better if you always study in the same place and have all of your materials handy so you don't waste any of your precious study time hunting for something. If your study area is outside your own home, you might want to pack up a separate backpack with all of your study tools so you know you'll always have them with you.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Create-Study-Plans-Step-1-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Create Study Plans Step 1 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/f6/Create-Study-Plans-Step-1-Version-2.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-1-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Think about your own needs—everyone's ideal study environment will be different! If you need absolute quiet with no distractions, you might find it best to study in a carrel in the library. But if you need a certain level of ambient noise and movement in the background, a café might be a better choice.<sup id=\"_ref-15\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 15\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-15\">[15]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Create-Study-Plans&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>The right study environment for you will depend on what type of learner you are. For example, if you're a visual learner, you might work best in an environment with a lot of color and brightness. If you're a kinesthetic learner, you might work best in a place where you can get up, move around, and write things down on a whiteboard.<sup id=\"_ref-16\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 16\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-16\">[16]</a></sup></li> \n  <li>Studying with a friend or group can help you stay motivated.<sup id=\"_ref-17\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 17\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-17\">[17]</a></sup></li> \n  <li>Use short bursts of time between classes to quickly review your notes or go through flashcards.<sup id=\"_ref-18\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 18\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Create-Study-Plans#_note-18\">[18]</a></sup></li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" 28px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-8-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn75@2020_6/2021/04/12/16-44-09-737_85fd6f2532063f28.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/96/Create-Study-Plans-Step-9.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-9.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn15@2020_6/2021/04/12/16-43-48-967_6392b52c45439b86.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/05/Create-Study-Plans-Step-10.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-10.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn91@2020_6/2021/04/12/16-43-48-941_87b346657710c94a.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/71/Create-Study-Plans-Step-11.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-11.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn11@2020_1/2021/04/12/16-43-48-072_15a68430bbc54aaa.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/34/Create-Study-Plans-Step-12.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-12.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn23@2020_2/2021/04/12/16-43-49-486_fd272c80e4a87158.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/43/Create-Study-Plans-Step-14.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-14.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn36@2020_3/2021/04/12/16-44-05-034_ffbeaf289611cbe2.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/02/Create-Study-Plans-Step-13.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-13.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn7@2020_4/2021/04/12/16-43-47-551_4c2353886cc079e9.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/f6/Create-Study-Plans-Step-1-Version-2.jpg/aid1882994-v4-728px-Create-Study-Plans-Step-1-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn95@2020_3/2021/04/12/16-43-47-561_9530b292039ad8d9.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1618245807265},{"createdTime":"2021-04-13 00:43:27","updatedTime":"2021-04-13 00:43:27","title":"How to Cook Chips in an Airfryer","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>The air fryer is a quick and healthy way to make many of your favorite snacks. Since it uses air to fry instead of oil, you can enjoy air-fried chips without any of the guilt of regular chips. Even better, there are many different types of chips that you can make. Try regular or sweet potatoes, beets, kale, or even tortilla chips. Whatever type you choose, you can add tons of flavor with your favorite spices and even some tasty dips. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Ingredients\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Ingredients\">Ingredients</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Potato Chips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Potato-Chips\">Potato Chips</span></h3> \n <ul>\n  <li>2 full-sized potatoes</li> \n  <li>Olive oil</li> \n  <li>Salt</li> \n  <li>Pepper</li> \n  <li>Any additional seasonings desired</li>\n </ul> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Beet Chips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Beet-Chips\">Beet Chips</span></h3> \n <ul>\n  <li>2-3 beets</li> \n  <li>Olive oil</li> \n  <li>Salt</li> \n  <li>Pepper</li> \n  <li>Any additional seasonings desired</li>\n </ul> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Kale Chips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Kale-Chips\">Kale Chips</span></h3> \n <ul>\n  <li>of kale leaves</li> \n  <li>Olive oil</li> \n  <li>Salt</li> \n  <li>Pepper</li>\n </ul> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Tortilla Chips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tortilla-Chips\">Tortilla Chips</span></h3> \n <ul>\n  <li>1 package medium tortillas</li> \n  <li>Olive oil</li> \n  <li>Salt</li> \n  <li>Pepper</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: Potato Chips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Potato-Chips_2\">Potato Chips</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Preheat the air fryer to about . Check the manual that came with your air fryer for a list of the recommended temperatures and times. If there is an included recipe for chips, follow those guidelines for the temperature. If not, go ahead and just set it to to preheat. Air fryers vary, but this temperature is pretty standard for chips.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-1.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Chips in an Airfryer Step 1.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/55/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-1.jpg/aid12189881-v4-728px-Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-1.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>It usually takes about 10 minutes for an air fryer to heat up.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Slice 2 potatoes to about using a knife or <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Use-a-Mandoline\" title=\"Use a Mandoline\">mandoline</a>. Potatoes and sweet potatoes both make delicious chips in the air fryer. You can choose your favorite or make a mixture. Some good choices include russets and Yukon Golds. Plan to use about 1 potato per person, but feel free to make a little extra for leftover snacks.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>There’s no need to peel the potatoes, but if you want to, go ahead and do that before slicing them.</li> \n    <li>Scrub your potatoes with water to get any dirt off and then place them on a cutting board.</li> \n    <li>You want them to be pretty thin so that they’ll get nice and crispy. If you have a mandoline, use that to help you get a thin, uniform cut.</li> \n    <li>If you don’t have a mandoline, that’s totally fine. Just use a sharp chef’s nice to thinly slice up your potatoes.</li> \n    <li>Don't use baby potatoes to make chips. They're just not big enough to make good chips.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Toss the potatoes with of oil and 1 tsp (6 g) of salt in a medium bowl. Place your potatoes in a bowl that is big enough for you to have room to shake the potatoes up. Now’s your chance to add your favorite flavors! Spritz the chips with a little cooking spray or olive oil spray so that spices will stick to them. If you want to keep it simple, just add a pinch of salt, shake, and you’re ready to air fry.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you don't have an oil mister, that's totally fine. Just sprinkle about of olive oil over the sliced potatoes.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Cook the chips for 22-30 minutes, tossing every 5 minutes. Now you’re ready to cook! If your air fryer has a basket, place the chips in it. They don’t have to be in 1 layer. If you have an air fryer with a tray, place your potatoes on the tray, making sure to only have 1 layer. The total cooking time is 30 minutes for regular potatoes, but you’ll need to flip the chips every 5 minutes to make sure they cook evenly.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Sweet potatoes cook more quickly, so they typically only take about 22 minutes.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup></li> \n    <li>If the chips are on a tray, use tongs to flip them over. If you have a basket, you can just take the basket out and give it a good shake every 5 minutes to rotate the chips. Since chips on baskets and trays cook a little differently, just remember it's fine to have a little overlap in the basket, but best to just make 1 even layer on a tray.</li> \n    <li>If you have a small air fryer or are making a lot of chips, you might have to cook in batches. Remember, you never want to overcrowd your air fryer, no matter what you’ve got cooking. If the chips are completely covering one another, you have too many in the basket or on the tray.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Take the chips out of the fryer when they’re crispy and let them cool. Check on the chips when they’re done cooking to see if they look and feel crispy enough for you. If you want them extra crispy, give them a few more minutes to fry. Carefully take them out of the fryer and let them rest for a few minutes on a paper towel. <sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Chips in an Airfryer Step 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/9e/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-5.jpg/aid12189881-v4-728px-Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>The paper towel will soak up any extra oil as the chips cool.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Season the chips again after cooking for added flavor. Now for the really fun part. You can add any flavors you like, so feel free to get creative. If you want a little spice, try adding some cayenne pepper. For a smoky taste, add a little cumin. Sweet potato chips might even be good with a little cinnamon and sugar.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Chips in an Airfryer Step 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/60/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-6.jpg/aid12189881-v4-728px-Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Other ideas include garlic salt, Italian seasoning, and ranch seasoning.</li> \n    <li>You could splash the chips with a little bit of malt vinegar or even balsamic vinegar if you like them a little tangy.</li> \n    <li>If you have any leftovers, store them in an airtight container at room temperature for up to 2 days.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8\" title=\"Edit section: Beet Chips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Beet-Chips_2\">Beet Chips</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Set the air fryer to about and let it preheat. The temperature might depend on your air fryer, but is pretty standard. Set your air fryer to that temp and let it heat up for about 10 minutes. Many air fryers will indicate with either a light or a beep when they are ready.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Chips in an Airfryer Step 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/74/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-7.jpg/aid12189881-v4-728px-Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If your air fryer manual recommends a different temperature for chips, use that temperature instead.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Cut 2-3 beets to about with a mandoline. You can use golden or purple beets, whichever you prefer. A mixture of the 2 is also great. If your beets are on the smaller side, you probably need 3 of them to make enough for 2 people. Otherwise, 2 will be fine. Plan to use a beet per person. Using your mandoline, slice the beets thinly so that you’ll be able to get crispy chips.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-8.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Chips in an Airfryer Step 8.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/1e/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-8.jpg/aid12189881-v4-728px-Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-8.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can use a sharp chef’s knife if you don’t have a mandoline.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Toss the beets with of olive oil and 1 tsp (6 g) each of salt and pepper. Place the beets in a medium bowl and spritz them with a little oil, just enough to dampen them a bit. If you have an olive oil mister, that will work perfectly. Otherwise, you can use cooking spray or just add a small splash of any type of oil you like (avocado, peanut, etc.). Add a little salt and pepper and shake the bowl a bit to make sure all of the beets are covered.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Cook the beet chips for 30 minutes, shaking the basket every 5 minutes. Place beets in the air fryer basket or on the cooking tray. It’s okay if they overlap in the basket a little; just make sure they’re not overcrowded. If any chips are completely covered by others, you have too many chips cooking at the same time. You’ll cook them for about 30 minutes total, but pause the timer every five minutes to either shake the basket or use tongs to flip the beets.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Frequently rotating the beets will ensure that they cook nice and evenly.</li> \n    <li>If you like your beet chips extra crispy, add a couple of additional minutes to the cooking time.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Serve immediately and save leftovers in an airtight container for 2 days. Take the beets out of the air fryer and place them in a bowl or on a plate. You can either eat them right away or let them cool for a few minutes. If you have leftovers, store them in an airtight container at room temperature for up to 2 days.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-11.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Chips in an Airfryer Step 11.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/fc/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-11.jpg/aid12189881-v4-728px-Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-11.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Beet chips are yummy on their own, but you could also serve them with your favorite dip to boost the flavor even more. A dill dip or hummus would be delicious with beet chips.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9\" title=\"Edit section: Kale Chips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Kale-Chips_2\">Kale Chips</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Turn on the air fryer and preheat it to . Air fryers take a few minutes to get hot, so give make sure you allow time for it to get up to the correct temperature. Go ahead and set it to while you get the kale ready. <sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-12.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Chips in an Airfryer Step 12.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/3f/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-12.jpg/aid12189881-v4-728px-Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-12.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Wash and tear of kale leaves into small pieces. This will make enough kale chips for 2 servings. If you would like to make extra, simply add some more kale. After you've washed the kale, tear it into bite-sized pieces. <sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Massage of olive oil into the kale leaves to make them tender. Kale can be a little bitter and rough if you don't massage the leaves a bit before cooking. Add a small splash of olive oil onto the leaves and use your hands to rub it gently into the kale. This just takes a few seconds but will definitely help you make the most delicious kale chips.<sup id=\"_ref-15\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 15\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-15\">[15]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Season the kale with 1 tsp (6 g) each of salt and pepper. After the oil is rubbed in, sprinkle the kale with your favorite seasonings. Keep it simple with salt and pepper, or jazz it up a bit with an Everything Bagel seasoning.<sup id=\"_ref-16\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 16\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-16\">[16]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can add any other flavors you like, too. Red pepper flakes will give the kale a nice kick, for example. Just season according to your own taste preferences.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Cook the kale leaves in batches at for 6 minutes. The kale will shrink quite a bit, but takes up a lot of room in the air fryer. Place about 1/3 of the kale into the basket and cook for 6 minutes. Shake the basket every 2 minutes to make sure the chips cook evenly. If you can't shake the kale leaves, you have too many in the basket. Take some out to give the chips more room to cook evenly.<sup id=\"_ref-17\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 17\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-17\">[17]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If your air fryer has a tray, that's fine. Just spread the kale chips in 1 even layer to cook.</li> \n    <li>Repeat this process until you've cooked all of the kale.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Remove chips when they are crispy and serve immediately. Once the chips are cooked the way you like them, take them out of the air fryer and place them in a bowl or on a plate. They taste best when hot, so sprinkle with a little more salt to add extra flavor and serve them up. You can season them according to your taste.<sup id=\"_ref-18\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 18\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-18\">[18]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-17.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Chips in an Airfryer Step 17.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/d2/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-17.jpg/aid12189881-v4-728px-Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-17.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you do happen to have leftovers, you can store them in an airtight container at room temperature for up to 2 days.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10\" title=\"Edit section: Tortilla Chips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tortilla-Chips_2\">Tortilla Chips</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Turn the air fryer to and let it preheat. Most air fryers will make delicious tortilla chips when you set the temp to around . If your manual offers different guidelines, you should use those instead. Allow your air fryer to preheat for about 10 minutes so that it’s nice and toasty when you’re ready to fry up the tortillas.<sup id=\"_ref-19\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 19\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-19\">[19]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-18.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Chips in an Airfryer Step 18.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/28/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-18.jpg/aid12189881-v4-728px-Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-18.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Cut 6 tortillas into triangles. The medium-sized tortillas work really well for chips, so grab a package of those (they will typically say medium or soft taco size on the package). 6 tortillas will make enough chips for 2-3 people; if you’re cooking for a crowd you can add extra. Stack the tortillas on top of each other and cut them into quarters. That easily turns them into triangles.<sup id=\"_ref-20\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 20\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-20\">[20]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>A pizza cutter is the perfect tool to use for cutting the tortillas. If you don’t have one, a knife will work fine, too.</li> \n    <li>You can use any type of tortillas you like. Corn, flour, and whole wheat are all great options.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Spray or brush the tortillas with of oil and sprinkle with 1 tsp (6 g) of salt. You can use any type of oil that you like. Olive, canola, and avocado oil are all great choices. Spritz the tortillas or use a pastry brush to lightly cover them with oil. Sprinkle on a little salt and you’re ready to cook.<sup id=\"_ref-21\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 21\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-21\">[21]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can add any other seasonings that you like, too. Garlic salt and cumin are good options. Sprinkle on as much as you like!</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Cook the chips in the basket for 4-6 minutes or until crispy. Put the tortillas in the basket or on the tray of the air fryer. It’s fine if they overlap, just make sure not to completely cover any of them with other chips. Start the air fryer and then check the chips after 4 minutes. If you’d like them a little crispier, go ahead and flip them over and cook for a couple more minutes.<sup id=\"_ref-22\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 22\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-22\">[22]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-21.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Chips in an Airfryer Step 21.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/bb/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-21.jpg/aid12189881-v4-728px-Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-21.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Serve with your favorite salsa or dip. Remove the chips from the air fryer and place them in a bowl. You can eat them plain, but they taste awesome when you pair them with a dip. Some tasty choices are:<sup id=\"_ref-23\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 23\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer#_note-23\">[23]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-22.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Chips in an Airfryer Step 22.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/fb/Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-22.jpg/aid12189881-v4-728px-Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer-Step-22.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Salsa</li> \n    <li>Guacamole</li> \n    <li>Hummus</li> \n    <li>Bean dip</li> \n    <li>You can save leftover chips in an airtight container at room temperature for about 2 days.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11\" title=\"Edit section: Video\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Video\">Video</span></h2> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Every air fryer is different, so it might take a couple of tries to figure out how long you like to cook your chips.</li> \n  <li>Flavor options for chips are endless, so play around with spices and herbs until you find your favorite.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Chips-in-an-Airfryer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13\" title=\"Edit section: Things You'll Need\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span id=\"Things-You'll-Need\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Things-You.27ll-Need\">Things You'll Need</span></h2> \n <p>Air fryer </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" class=\"mw-parser-output\"><p>This wikiHow will teach you how to retrieve deleted Memories on Snapchat using Recoverit with your Android phone or tablet, which will allow you to access deleted images on your Android. If you use an iPhone or iPad, you can use iCloud if you have that set up to <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Restore-from-iCloud\" title=\"Restore from iCloud\">restore a backup</a>. However, if you keep a recent backup of your Snapchat account from Snapchat's settings, you'll be able to find your deleted Memories within that backup.\n</p>\n<h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat&#38;action=edit&#38;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2>\n<ol><li>Go to the Recoverit download page and click the Windows or macOS  button. You can only do this with an Android phone or tablet since the file system works differently for iOS phones and tablets. There are two buttons displaying the Windows logo or macOS to indicate which button leads to which download.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-1.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Retrieve Deleted Memories on Snapchat Step 1.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/90/Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-1.jpg/aid12513242-v4-728px-Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-1.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div>\n<ul><li>Save the appropriate download file, then open it once it has finished downloading. Many browsers, like Chrome, give you a notification at the bottom of the window that you can click to open the downloaded file.</li>\n<li>Once you open the downloaded file, follow the on-screen instructions to install Recoverit. For Mac users, this may include dragging and dropping an application from the downloaded file into the Applications folder in Finder. Windows users click <b>Yes</b> and <b>Install</b> through the pop-up prompts until installation is complete.</li></ul></li>\n<li>Connect your Android to your computer via USB cable. Your Android should have come with a cable that can connect your Android and computer; you might have to change the permissions from your Android to allow the USB connection to file transfer.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Retrieve Deleted Memories on Snapchat Step 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/ae/Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-2.jpg/aid12513242-v4-728px-Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"529\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div></li>\n<li>Open Recoverit (if it does not open automatically). You'll find this in the Start menu in Windows or the Applications folder in Finder in Mac.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-3.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Retrieve Deleted Memories on Snapchat Step 3.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/63/Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-3.jpg/aid12513242-v4-728px-Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-3.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div></li>\n<li>Click your Android from the list of \"External Devices.<b>\"</b> It should be the second grouping of options in the menu.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Retrieve Deleted Memories on Snapchat Step 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/d4/Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-4.jpg/aid12513242-v4-728px-Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div></li>\n<li>Look for your Snapchat Memories. Any images that you took on your Android will display as the software scans and finds them. Double-click the file names to see a preview of the image.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Retrieve Deleted Memories on Snapchat Step 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/26/Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-5.jpg/aid12513242-v4-728px-Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div></li>\n<li>Click . Once you recover the image, it'll save to your computer.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Retrieve-Deleted-Memories-on-Snapchat-Step-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Retrieve Deleted Memories on Snapchat Step 6.jpg\"
